UKRAINE:

Equivalence between medicines registered in Ukraine and other countries. Information for healthcare professionals and patients

To support and facilitate the provision of healthcare and medicines to refugees from Ukraine

УКРАЇНА:

Еквівалентність лікарських засобів, зареєстрованих в Україні та інших країнах. Інформація для працівників охорони здоров'я та пацієнтів

Для підтримки надання медичної допомоги та забезпечення лікарськими засобами біженців з України

Version 2: 27 April 2022

Introduction / Aim of this document

According to the United Nations Refugee Agency (UNHCR), the current war in Ukraine has led over 4.6 million people living in Ukraine to seek refuge in other countries, as of 12 April 2022 (over 10% of the population of Ukraine). In addition to a safe place to live, refugees require healthcare and the use of medicines, often for the continuation of treatments in people living with chronic or long‐term conditions.

To support the provision of healthcare and medicines in the host countries, and as part of FIP’s response to the appeals of our member organisation, the All‐Ukrainian Pharmaceutical Chamber, FIP has developed the tables of equivalence between medicines registered in Ukraine and those available in other countries, published in this document. This is meant to facilitate the provision of (pharmaceutical) care to refugees and also to support healthcare professionals providing care to them. We are prioritising medicines for the following chronic non‐communicable diseases that require continuation of treatment: asthma & COPD, mental health, cardiovascular diseases and diabetes, but also oral contraceptives. This list may be expanded as necessary.

The tables in this publication include the ATC classification and INN of selected medicines, their name in Ukrainian language (both in Cyrillic and Latin alphabets), and also brand names, as well as the dosage form (in both languages) and information about the manufacturer. Additionally, links are provided for additional information/advice for patients in Ukrainian. Further details about these medicines and their clinical use can be readily found in other sources.

These tables may be used in conjunction with the FIP pictograms software to facilitate the provision of advice to patients when there isn't a common language.

FIP is grateful to Associate Professor Dr Iryna Vlasenko, an academic pharmacist from Ukraine, for her invaluable and selfless collaboration in compiling this information. Dr Vlasenko is a Member of the European Medicine Agency (EMA)’s Working Party with Patients and Consumers, a member of the Steering Group of the European Network of Centres for Pharmacoepidemiology and Pharmacovigilance, and a vice president of the International Federation on Diabetes.

FIP is also grateful to Prof. Oleg Devinyak, Chair of the Department of Pharmaceutical Sciences of Uzhhorod National University, Ukraine, and his team formed by Fedaka Katerina, Voitovych Irina, Peleshkei Zita and Plovayko Tatiana, for their noble collaboration on this initiative under dire circumstances.

How to use this document

  1. The tables are sorted in alphabetical order of the INN/active ingredient in English.

  2. You may search for a medicine by INN (active ingredient) or by brand name in English or Ukrainian, in Cyrillic or Latin characters. Should you need to search for a medicine name in Cyrillic characters but you do not have a Cyrillic keyboard, you may use the table in Appendix 1 for the transliteration between the two alphabets.

  3. Should you wish to provide information to patients in Ukrainian language, links are provided for further details.

Other useful resources

  • Official registry of medicines available on the website of the Ukrainian Ministry of Health: http://www.drlz.com.ua/

  • Regulatory documents of the Ministry of Health of Ukraine: https://mozdocs.kiev.ua/

  • Medicines Compendium of Ukraine: https://compendium.com.ua/

  • IQVIA database: https://ukrainemedlist.solutions.iqvia.com/

  • Apps like Apple World Drugs Converter or Apple Traveler’s Pharmacy ‐ Equivalent Medications

Yahotyn Yaroshenko Kostiantyn Znamianka

Feodosiia

Notes: 1. Combination of letters "зг" is transliterated as "zgh" (e.g., Згорани – Zghorany,

Розгон Rozghon) as opposed to "zh" – the equivalent of the Ukrainian letter "ж".

  1. Soft sign and the apostrophe are not reproduced in Latin.

  2. Transliteration of first and last names of individuals and geographical names is carried out by way of

letter‐for‐letter representation in Latin.
